(۹۷) إِنَّ الْخُلْعَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْبَيْعِ فِي جَانِبِ الْمَرْأَةِ وَبِمَنْزِلَةِ الْيَمِينِ فِي جَانِبِ الرَّجُلِ. ترجمہ: خلع عورت کی طرف سے بمنزلہ بیع کے ہے اور مرد کی طرف سے بمنزلہ یمین کے ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ خلع عورت کے حق میں بمنزلہ بیع کے ہے، لہذا جو چیزیں بیع میں درست ہوتی ہیں وہ خلع میں بھی عورت کی طرف سے درست ہوں گی، اور مرد کے حق میں بمنزلہ یمین کے ہے، لہذا مرد کے جانب سے جو احکام یمین کے ہیں ان کا یہاں بھی لحاظ رکھا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر شوہر نے خلع میں اپنے لئے اختیار رکھا بایں طور کہ شوہر نے بیوی سے یہ کہا: انتِ طَالِقٌ بِأَلْفِ عَلَى أَنِّي بِالْخِيَارِ (کہ تجھے طلاق ہے ہزار پر بشرطیکہ مجھے اختیار ہوگا) اور بیوی نے یہ قبول بھی کر لیا تو مرد کے حق میں اختیار باطل ہوگا، اس لئے کہ خلع مرد کی طرف سے بمنزلہ یمین کے ہے اور یمین میں اختیار کی شرط لگانا درست نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر عورت کے لئے اختیار کی شرط لگائی جائے بایں طور کہ شوہر یہ کہے: انتِ طَالِقٌ بِأَلْفِ عَلَى أَنَّكِ بِالْخِيَارِ تو یہ درست ہے، کیونکہ خلع عورت کی طرف سے بمنزلہ بیع کے ہے اور بیع میں اختیار کی شرط لگانا درست ہے۔ جس طرح بیع میں رجوع کرنا صحیح ہوتا ہے اور بیع ماورائے مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہوتی، اسی طرح خلع میں بھی رجوع کرنا صحیح ہے اور خلع بھی ماورائے مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہے۔ بیع میں خیار کی شرط لگانا درست ہے اس لئے خلع میں بھی خیار کی شرط لگانا درست ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر شوہر کے لئے خیار شرط ہو تو درست نہیں ہے، کیونکہ شوہر کی جانب میں خلع یمین ہے، اس لئے شوہر نہ خلع کرنے کے بعد رجوع کر سکتا ہے اور نہ ہی مجلس تک منحصر رہتا ہے، بلکہ شوہر کے حق میں ماورائے مجلس پر موقوف بھی رہتا ہے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ جانب زوج میں خلع یمین ہے اور ایمان اور قسموں میں خیار نہیں ہوتا، اس لئے شوہر کے لئے خیار نہیں ہوگا۔
(قَوْلُهُ وَصَحْ خِيَارُ الشَّرْطِ لَهَا لَا لَهُ) لِمَا قَدَّمْنَا أَنَّهُ مُعَاوَضَةٌ مِنْ جِهَتِهَا، وَيَمِينٌ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ، وَلِذَا صَحْ رُجُوعُهَا قَبْلَ الْقَبُولِ، وَلَا تَصِحُ إِضَافَتُهَا، وَتَعْلِيقُهَا بِالشَّرْطِ، وَلَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى مَا وَرَاءَ الْمَجْلِسِ، وَانْعَكَسَتُ الْأحْكَامُ مِنْ جَانِبِهِ، وَهُمَا مَنَعَاهُ مِنْ جَانِبِهَا أَيْضًا نَظَرًا إِلَى جَانِبِ الْيَمِينِ، وَالْحَقُّ مَا قَالَهُ الْإِمَامُ أَطْلَقَهُ فَشَمِلَ الْخُلُعَ وَالطَّلَاقَ عَلَى مَالِ ، وَيَتَفَرَّعُ عَلَى هَذَا الْأَصْلِ مَسَائِلُ مِنْهَا مَا لَوْ قَالَ أَنَّت طَالِقٌ عَلَى أَلْفِ عَلَى أَنِّى بِالْخِيَارِ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فَقَبِلَتْ بَطَلَ الْخِيَارُ، وَوَقَعَ الطَّلَاقُ، وَمِنْهَا مَا لَوْ قَالَ أَنْت طَالِقٌ عَلَى أَلْفِ عَلَى أَنَّكَ بِالْخِيَارِ ثَلاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فَقَبِلَتْ إِنْ رَدَّتُ الطَّلَاقَ فِي الأَيَّامِ الثَّلاثَةِ بَطَلَ الطَّلَاقُ، وَإِنْ اخْتَارَتْ الطَّلَاقَ فِى الأَيَّامِ الثَّلَاثَةِ وَقَعَ، وَوَجَبَ الْأَلْفُ لَهُ، وَعِنْدَهُمَا الطَّلَاقُ وَاقِعٌ فِى الْوَجْهَيْنِ ، وَالْمَالُ لَازِمٌ عَلَيْهَا، وَالْخِيَارُ بَاطِلٌ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ.
البحر الرائق: كتاب الطلاق، باب الخلع، ج ۴، ص ۹۲ ، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
(97) Indeed, khul' is like sale from the woman's side and like an oath from the man's side. Translation: Khul' is like sale from the woman's side and like an oath from the man's side. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that khul' is like a sale from the woman's perspective, therefore whatever is valid in a sale will be valid from the woman's side in khul', and from the man's side it is like an oath, therefore the rulings of oaths will be observed here from the man's side. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the principle, is stating that if the husband stipulates an option for himself in khul' such that he says to his wife: 'You are divorced for a thousand on condition that I have the option' and she accepts, then the option becomes void for the man, because khul' is like an oath from the man's side and stipulating an option in an oath is not valid. And if an option is stipulated for the woman such that the husband says: 'You are divorced for a thousand on condition that you have the option', then this is valid, because khul' is like a sale from the woman's side and stipulating an option in a sale is valid. Just as retracting is valid in a sale and the sale is not suspended beyond the session, similarly retracting is valid in khul' and khul' is not suspended beyond the session. Stipulating an option in a sale is valid, therefore stipulating an option in khul' is also valid. On the contrary, if an option is stipulated for the husband, it is not valid, because from the husband's side khul' is an oath, so the husband can neither retract after khul' nor is it confined to the session; rather, from the husband's side it is suspended beyond the session. So it is known that from the husband's side khul' is an oath, and in oaths and vows there is no option, therefore there will be no option for the husband.
(His statement: 'And the stipulation of option is valid for her, not for him') because we have presented that it is an exchange from her side and an oath from his side, therefore her retraction before acceptance is valid, and it is not valid to add or suspend it by condition, and it does not stop beyond the session, and the rulings are reversed from his side. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) forbade it from her side as well, considering the side of the oath, but the truth is what the Imam said. He stated it absolutely, so it includes khul' and divorce for money. And from this principle branch issues, among them if he said: 'You are divorced for a thousand on condition that I have the option for three days' and she accepted, the option becomes void and divorce occurs. And among them if he said: 'You are divorced for a thousand on condition that you have the option for three days' and she accepted, then if she rejects the divorce within the three days, the divorce becomes void; and if she chooses the divorce within the three days, it occurs and the thousand becomes obligatory for him. According to them (Sahibayn), the divorce occurs in both cases, and the money is binding on her, and the option is void in both cases.
Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Book of Divorce, Chapter of Khul', vol. 4, p. 92, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami)
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage introduces a foundational principle of Hanafi fiqh regarding khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with compensation). The principle is: 'Indeed, khul' is like a sale from the woman's side and like an oath from the man's side.' This is a definition_ruling that distinguishes the nature of the contract for each party. The commentary explains that because it is like a sale for the woman, all rules of sale apply to her, including the validity of stipulating an option (خيار الشرط). For the man, it is like an oath, so no option is valid for him, and the divorce is binding immediately without the possibility of retraction or suspension. The author of Hidayah applies this principle: if the husband stipulates an option for himself (e.g., 'You are divorced for a thousand on condition that I have the option'), the option is void because an oath does not admit options. However, if the woman is given the option, it is valid because from her side it is a sale, and in sales, options are valid. The passage then cites the Arabic text from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, which further elaborates: The correct position is that the stipulation of option is valid for her but not for him. This is based on the nature of khul' as an exchange for her and an oath for him. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagreed and held that even the woman's option is void, considering the oath side to be dominant. But the text declares that the truth is with Imam Abu Hanifa. Then examples are given: If the husband says 'You are divorced for a thousand on condition that I have the option for three days' and she accepts, the option is void and divorce occurs immediately. If the condition is for her option, she has a choice within three days: she can reject the divorce (making it void) or accept it (making it binding and she owes the thousand). According to the Sahibayn, in both cases divorce occurs and money is due, and the option is void. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the Imam. This principle has many branch cases. The key takeaway is that in khul', the woman's position is that of a seller, allowing her to enjoy rights like option and retraction before acceptance; the man's position is like that of one who makes an oath, so his divorce is binding and cannot include conditions that contradict the nature of an oath.

Key Terms
خیار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated by either party in a contract to cancel or confirm within a specified period.
معاوضہ (mu'awadah): Exchange contract where consideration is given for the right of divorce.
یمین (yamin): Oath or vow that binds the person without room for conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced for a thousand on condition that I have the option for three days' and she accepts, what is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The option is valid, so the husband can cancel within three days.
B) The option is void, and divorce occurs immediately.
C) The divorce does not occur until the three days pass.
D) The option is valid only if the wife also agrees.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khul' combines sale and oath rules: options (khiyar al-shart) are valid for the wife but not for the husband.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Khiyar al-Shart in Khul' and Talaq 'ala Mal
Explaining the ruling on stipulating option in divorce for compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-shart in khul' and talaq 'ala mal, explain the dual nature of khul' (sale vs vow), and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Khul' is sale for the wife and vow for the husband – option is valid only for her.

In this lesson, we explore a nuanced rule in Hanafi fiqh: can a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) be attached to a khul' or divorce for compensation? The answer depends on which party stipulates it, because khul' has a dual nature. From the husband's side it is a dissolutive vow (yamin), but from the wife's side it is a compensatory transaction (mu'awada). The great Imam Abu Hanifa ruled that the option is valid for the wife but void for the husband, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagreed. The passage clarifies this ikhtilaf and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed issue
The act is stipulating a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) in a khul' or talaq 'ala mal. The dispute: is this condition valid for either party?
Remember that khul' is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the option is valid for the wife but invalid for the husband. His proof: from the wife's side, khul' is analogous to sale (bay'), which permits option; from the husband's side, it is analogous to a vow (yamin), which does not.
This is based on qiyas to two different origins (sale and vow).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the option is invalid for both parties. Their proof: they consider the vow aspect predominant on both sides, so no option can be attached.
They prioritize the husband's side's characterization (vow) over the wife's side's compensation.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference) given in the text
The text declares that the truth (al-haqq) is with Abu Hanifa. The reasoning: khul' is primarily a compensatory contract, and the wife's side is clearly analogous to sale, so her right to option is valid. The husband's side remains a vow, so his option is void.
The Sahibayn's view is marjuh (weaker) in this matter according to the author.
5
Apply the rule to branch cases
The text gives two examples: (1) Husband stipulates option for himself → option void, divorce occurs immediately. (2) Wife stipulates option for herself → she can reject within three days (divorce void) or accept (divorce binding). According to Sahibayn, in both cases divorce occurs immediately and payment is due.
This shows the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in when the divorce takes effect and who controls it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی طلاق ہے ہزار پر بشر طیکہ مجھے اختیار ہوگا اور بیوی نے یہ قبول بھی کر لیا تو مرد کے حق میں اختیار باطل ہوگا، اس لئے کہ ضلع مرد کی طرف سے بمنزلہ یمین کے ہے اور یمین میں اختیار کی شرط لگانا درست نہیں ہے اور اگر عورت کے لئے اختیار کی شرط لگائی جائے بایں طور کہ شوہر یہ کہئے انتِ طَالِقٌ بِأَلْفِ عَلَى أَنَّكِ بِالْخِيَارِ تو یہ درست ہے، کیونکہ ضلع عورت کی طرف سے بمنزلہ بیع کے ہے اور بیچ میں اختیار کی شرط لگانا درست ہے، جس طرح بیچ میں رجوع کرنا صحیح ہوتا ہے اور بیج ماورائے مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہوتی ، اسی طرح ضلع میں بھی رجوع کرنا صحیح ہے اور ضلع بھی ماورائے مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہے، بیج میں خیار کی شرط لگانا درست ہے اس لئے ضلع میں بھی خیار کی شرط لگانا درست ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر شوہر کے لئے خیار شرط ہو تو درست نہیں ہے، کیونکہ شوہر کی جانب میں ضلع یمین ہے، اس لئے شوہر نہ ضلع کرنے کے بعد رجوع کر سکتا ہے اور نہ ہی مجلس تک منحصر رہتا ہے، بلکہ شوہر کے حق میں ماورائے مجلس پر موقوف بھی رہتا ہے،معلوم ہوا کہ جانب زوج میں خلع یمین ہے اور ایمان اور قسموں میں خیار نہیں ہوتا ، اس لئے شوہر کے لئے خیار نہیں ہوگا۔
(قَوْلُهُ وَصَحْ خِيَارُ الشَّرْطِ لَهَا لَا لَهُ) لِمَا قَدَّمْنَا أَنَّهُ مُعَاوَضَةٌ مِنْ جِهَتِهَا، وَيَمِينٌ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ، وَلِذَا صَحْ رُجُوعُهَا قَبْلَ الْقَبُولِ، وَلَا تَصِحُ إِضَافَتُهَا، وَتَعْلِيقُهَا بِالشَّرْطِ، وَلَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى مَا وَرَاءَ الْمَجْلِسِ، وَانْعَكَسَتُ الْأحْكَامُ مِنْ جَانِبِهِ، وَهُمَا مَنَعَاهُ مِنْ جَانِبِهَا أَيْضًا نَظَرًا إِلَى جَانِبِ الْيَمِينِ، وَالْحَقُّ مَا قَالَهُ الْإِمَامُ أَطْلَقَهُ فَشَمِلَ الْخُلُعَ وَالطَّلَاقَ عَلَى مَالِ ، وَيَتَفَرَّعُ عَلَى هَذَا الْأَصْلِ مَسَائِلُ مِنْهَا مَا لَوْ قَالَ أَنَّت طَالِقٌ عَلَى أَلْفِ عَلَى أَنِّى بِالْخِيَارِ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فَقَبِلَتْ بَطَلَ الْخِيَارُ، وَوَقَعَ الطَّلَاقُ، وَمِنْهَا مَا لَوْ قَالَ أَنْت طَالِقٌ عَلَى أَلْفِ عَلَى أَنَّكَ بِالْخِيَارِ ثَلاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فَقَبِلَتْ إِنْ رَدَّتُ الطَّلَاقَ فِي الأَيَّامِ الثَّلاثَةِ بَطَلَ الطَّلَاقُ، وَإِنْ اخْتَارَتْ الطَّلَاقَ فِى الأَيَّامِ الثَّلَاثَةِ وَقَعَ، وَوَجَبَ الْأَلْفُ لَهُ، وَعِنْدَهُمَا الطَّلَاقُ وَاقِعٌ فِى الْوَجْهَيْنِ ، وَالْمَالُ لَازِمٌ عَلَيْهَا، وَالْخِيَارُ بَاطِلٌ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ.
البحر الرائق: كتاب الطلاق، باب الخلع، ج ۴، ص ۹۲ ، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
Divorce is for one thousand on condition that I have the option, and the wife accepts it, then the option becomes void for the husband, because khul' from the husband's side is like a vow, and stipulating a condition of option in a vow is not valid. And if the condition of option is stipulated for the wife, in such a way that the husband says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have the option,' then it is valid, because khul' from the wife's side is like a sale, and stipulating a condition of option in a sale is valid. Just as revocation before acceptance is valid in a sale and sale is not suspended beyond the session, similarly revocation before acceptance is valid in khul' and khul' is not suspended beyond the session. Stipulating option in a sale is valid, thus stipulating option in khul' is valid. Conversely, if the option is stipulated for the husband, it is not valid, because from the husband's side khul' is a vow, so the husband can neither revoke after pronouncing khul' nor is it confined to the session; rather, it is suspended beyond the session for the husband. It is understood that from the husband's side khul' is a vow, and oaths and vows do not admit option, so the husband will not have the option.
(His statement: 'And the option of condition is valid for her, not for him.') Because we have stated that it is a compensation from her side and a vow from his side. For this reason, her revocation before acceptance is valid, but adding it and suspending it on a condition are not valid, and it is not suspended beyond the session. The rulings are reversed from his side. And they (the two) prohibited it from her side as well, considering the aspect of the vow. The truth is what the Imam said; he made it general, so it includes khul' and divorce for compensation. From this principle branch issues: among them, if he says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that I have the option for three days' and she accepts, the option becomes void and the divorce occurs. And among them, if he says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have the option for three days' and she accepts, if she rejects the divorce within the three days, the divorce becomes void, and if she chooses the divorce within the three days, it occurs and the thousand becomes obligatory for him. According to them (the two), the divorce occurs in both cases, the payment is obligatory on her, and the option is void in both cases. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Kitab al-Talaq, Bab al-Khul', vol. 4, p. 92, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami)
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage from Usool al-Hidayah discusses the ruling on stipulating a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) in a khul' or divorce for compensation (talaq 'ala mal). The author first explains the Urdu commentary: if the husband stipulates an option for himself, it is invalid because khul' from his side is analogous to a vow (yamin), and vows do not admit conditions of option. But if the condition is for the wife, it is valid because from the wife's side, khul' is analogous to a sale (bay'), and sales do admit conditions of option. This follows the Hanafi principle that khul' has a dual nature: it is a compensatory contract (mu'awada) from the wife's side and a dissolutive act akin to a vow from the husband's side. The Arabic text from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq confirms that Imam Abu Hanifa held this view, but the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disallowed the condition for the wife as well, arguing that the vow aspect predominates. The author sides with Abu Hanifa, stating that the truth (al-haqq) is what the Imam said. The passage then gives two examples: (1) if the husband says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that I have the option for three days,' and she accepts, the option is void and the divorce takes effect immediately. (2) If the condition is for the wife to have the option, and she accepts, then if she rejects within three days, the divorce is void; if she chooses it, the divorce occurs and she owes the one thousand. According to the Sahibayn, the divorce occurs in both cases and the payment is due, and the option is void. This difference has practical consequences: under Abu Hanifa's view, a wife can secure a right to reconsider that the husband cannot.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in return for compensation paid to the husband.
یمین (yamin): A vow or oath; in this context, the husband's pronouncement of khul' is treated like a vow that does not admit conditions of option.
بیع (bay'): Sale; used as analogy for the wife's side in khul' as a compensatory transaction.
خیار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option clause allowing one party to confirm or rescind the contract within a specified period.
طلاق علی مال (talaq 'ala mal): Divorce in return for payment by the wife, similar to khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that I have the option for three days,' and she accepts, what is the ruling?
A) The option is valid and the divorce is suspended.
B) The option becomes void and the divorce occurs immediately.
C) The divorce is void because the option was invalid.
D) The wife may choose to accept or reject within three days.

Key Takeaway
In khul' and talaq 'ala mal, khiyar al-shart is valid only for the wife (as in sale) and not for the husband (as in vow), according to Abu Hanifa's view which is the mufta bihi.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Divisibility of Manumission in Zihar Expiation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on manumission divisibility in zihar expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the divisibility of manumission in zihar expiation and apply the ruling to a scenario involving partial manumission.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: half a slave is not a whole; Sahibayn: half is whole—timing of intercourse decides expiation validity.

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi disagreement on a key fiqh principle: is manumission (i'taq) divisible or indivisible? The dispute surfaces in the context of zihar expiation, where the Quran requires freeing a slave before marital relations. The two companions (Sahibayn) hold that freeing half a slave legally equals freeing the whole, while Imam Abu Hanifa insists on complete manumission before intercourse. We will parse the reasoning and apply it to a concrete case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Disagreement
Read the principle: 'manumission is divisible according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them.' Understand that the core disagreement is whether freeing half a slave counts as freeing the entire slave legally.
The term 'tajazzi' means divisibility.
2
Locate the Quranic Evidence
The verse 58:3 'freeing a slave before they touch' sets a condition. Identify how each side uses this text to support their view.
Abu Hanifa focuses on 'raqabah' implying a whole slave; Sahibayn focus on the act of freeing, arguing that half is legally whole.
3
Apply to the Zihar Scenario
Work through the hypothetical: a man frees half a slave for zihar expiation, then has intercourse, then frees the other half. Determine the ruling under each position.
The timing of intercourse relative to full manumission is key.
4
Trace the Istinbat
Follow how each imam derives the ruling from the text and their usul principles. Note the role of 'urfi vs. shar'i meaning of 'freeing a slave'.
This is a usul-based dispute on the interpretation of 'raqabah'.
5
Identify the Thamara al-Khilaf
State the practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the expiation is invalid and a new slave must be freed; under Sahibayn, the expiation is valid. Know which position is mufta bihi (relied upon) in later fatwa.
Later Hanafi authorities tend to favor the Sahibayn's view, but the dispute remains known.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الْإِعْتَاقَ يَتَجَزَّى عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ خِلَافًا لَهُمَا.
ترجمہ: امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اعتاق منجزی ہوتا ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اعتاق منجزی نہیں ہوتا۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اعتناق یعنی غلام کو آزاد کرنے میں تجری ہوتی ہے یعنی قابل تقسیم ہے، لہذا انصف کو آزاد کرنا پھر دوسرے نصف کو آزاد کرنا ہے، جبکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک اعتاق غیر منجزی ہے یعنی قابل تقسیم نہیں ہے، لہذا نصف کا اعتناق کل کا اعتناق ہو گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر ظہار کرنے والے نے نصف غلام کفارہ ظہار میں آزاد کیا پھر اس بیوی سے جماع کیا جس کے ساتھ ظہار کیا تھا، پھر باقی نصف آزاد کر لیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ جائز نہیں ہوگا یعنی کفارہ ادا نہیں ہوگا، جبکہ صاحبین رحمہما اللہ کے نزدیک کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اعتاق متجری ہوتا ہے یعنی نصف کا آزاد کرنا کل کا آزاد کرنا نہیں ہے، لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں نصف غلام جماع کے بعد آزاد ہوا ہے جبکہ پورے غلام کو قبل الجماع آزاد کر نا نص مِنْ قَبْلِ أَنْ يَّتَمَاسًا (المجادلة: ۳) سے ثابت ہے اور صاحبین کے نزد یک چونکہ اعتاق میں تجری نہیں ہے، لہذا انصف کا آزاد کر نا کل کا آزاد کرنا ہے۔
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب الظهار، فصل فى الكفارة، ج ۲ ص ۴۲۰، ط: رحمانيه (قَوْلُهُ وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ نِصْفَ عَبْدِهِ عَنْ كَفَّارَتِهِ ثُمَّ جَامَعَ الَّتِى ظَاهَرَ مِنْهَا ثُمَّ أَعْتَقَ بَاقِيَهُ لَمْ يُجْزِ هَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ)، لأنَّ الْإِعْتَاقَ يَتَجَزَّأُ عِنْدَهُ وَشَرْطُ الْإِعْتَاقِ أَنْ يَكُونَ قَبْلَ الْمَسِيسِ بِالنَّصَّ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مِنْ قَبْلِ أَنْ يَتَمَاسًا وَإِعْتَاقُ النِّصْفِ حَصَلَ بَعْد الْمَسِيسِ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَجُوزُ، لأنَّ إعْتَاقَ النِّصْفِ عِنْدَهُمَا إِعْتَاقَ الْكُلِّ فَحَصَلَ إعْتَاقَ الْكُلِّ قَبْلَ الْمَسِيسِ وَإِذَا لَمْ يَجُرُ عِندَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ اسْتَأْنَفَ عِتْقَ رَقَبَةٍ أُخْرَى.
الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الظهار، كفارة الظهار، ج ۲ ص ۶۷، ط: المطبعة الخيرية
Indeed, manumission is divisible according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Translation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, manumission is divisible, and according to the two companions, manumission is not divisible. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that according to Imam Sahib, manumission (freeing a slave) allows division, i.e., it is subject to partition; therefore, freeing half then freeing the other half (is valid), while according to the two companions, manumission is not divisible, so freeing half is freeing the whole. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a person who has made zihar frees half a slave for the expiation, then has intercourse with the wife from whom he made zihar, then frees the remaining half, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this is not valid, i.e., the expiation is not fulfilled, while according to the two companions, the expiation is fulfilled. According to Imam Sahib, manumission is divisible, so freeing half is not freeing the whole; therefore in the mentioned case, half the slave was freed after intercourse, while freeing the entire slave must be before intercourse as established by the text 'from before they touch' (Quran 58:3). According to the two, since manumission is not divisible, freeing half is freeing the whole. Al-Hidayah, Book of Divorce, Chapter of Zihar, Section on Expiation, vol. 2 p. 420, Rahmaniyya edition: (His statement: And if he frees half his slave for his expiation, then has intercourse with the woman from whom he made zihar, then frees the remainder, this is not valid according to Abu Hanifa), because manumission is divisible with him, and the condition of manumission is that it be before intercourse by the text. Allah says: 'freeing a slave before they touch.' And freeing half occurred after intercourse. According to them (the two), it is valid, because freeing half according to them is freeing the whole, so freeing the whole occurred before intercourse. And if it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa, he should initiate freeing another slave. Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, Book of Zihar, Expiation of Zihar, vol. 2 p. 67, al-Khayriyya Press.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the divisibility of manumission (i'taq) in the context of zihar expiation. The principle stated is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, manumission is divisible (mutajazzi), meaning that freeing half a slave is not the same as freeing the entire slave. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), manumission is indivisible, so freeing half legally constitutes freeing the whole. The practical consequence is illustrated: a person who makes zihar must free a slave before intercourse. If he frees half a slave, then has intercourse, then frees the remaining half, Abu Hanifa rules the expiation invalid because half the slave was freed after intercourse, whereas the Sahibayn rule it valid because the half represented the whole and was freed before intercourse. Abu Hanifa's evidence is the Quranic verse 'min qabli an yatamassa' (before they touch), which requires complete manumission before intercourse. The Sahibayn interpret that because manumission is indivisible, half is equivalent to whole. The Hidayah author mentions this to clarify the ruling: if invalid per Abu Hanifa, a new slave must be freed. The reference to Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira confirms the authority of this ruling. This dispute affects the validity of expiation in zihar and other cases where manumission is required.

Key Terms
إِعْتَاق (i'taq): The act of freeing a slave; manumission.
تَجَزِّي (tajazzi): Divisibility; the property of being divisible into parts.
ظِهَار (zihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a man says to his wife 'You are to me like my mother's back'; requires expiation.
كَفَّارَة (kaffara): Expiation for committing a prohibited act, here for zihar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied upon) position in the Hanafi school, if a man frees half a slave before intercourse in zihar expiation and the other half after, his expiation is:
A) Invalid, because half is not whole.
B) Valid, because half equals whole.
C) Valid only if he intended to free the whole.
D) Invalid in all cases.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on manumission divisibility changes the ruling on zihar expiation validity when only half a slave is freed before intercourse.

The Meaning of It'am: Enabling Access vs. Ownership Transfer
Defines it'am and contrasts Hanafi-Shafi'i views on zihar expiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that it'am in zihar expiation does not require tamlik and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
It'am means enabling access to food; serving a meal fulfills the obligation.

This passage from Al-Hidayah defines the literal meaning of it'am and uses it to settle a key dispute in zihar expiation. The Hanafis argue that feeding the poor simply means making food available to them, not necessarily transferring ownership. You will learn how the Hanafi school relies on linguistic precision to distinguish it'am from other obligations like zakat, and why the Shafi'i analogy fails.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What does it'am mean according to the Hanafis? Identify the key term 'tamkin' (enabling access) and note that serving meals morning and evening suffices for zihar expiation.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it'am requires tamlik (ownership transfer). His proof is qiyas on zakat and fitr sadaqah, where tamlik is mandated.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i analogy: just as zakat and fitr require giving the poor ownership of food, so too should zihar expiation. What texts do they cite?
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis rebut by pointing to different Quranic wording: zakat uses 'ita' (giving) and 'ada' (paying) which imply tamlik, while zihar uses 'it'am' which means tamkin. Hence the analogy is invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? Under Hanafi ruling, one may invite the poor to a meal; under Shafi'i, one must hand over the food as possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اَلْإِطْعَامُ هُوَ حَقِيقَةٌ فِي التَّمْكِيْنِ مِنَ الطَّعَامِ.
ترجمہ: اطعام کے حقیقی معنی ہیں کھانے پر قدرت دینا۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اطعام حقیقت میں کہتے ہیں کھانے پر قدرت دینے کو یعنی جب کوئی آدمی کسی کو کھانے پر قدرت دیدیتا ہے تو اطعام کا معنی ثابت ہو جاتا ہے، یہی معنی یعنی کھانے پر قدرت دینا اباحت میں بھی پایا جاتا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر ظہار کرنے والے نے ساٹھ مسکین کو صبح و شام کھانا کھلایا تو کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ اطعام کا معنی کھانے پر قدرت دینا ہے اور جب مظاہر نے مساکین کو کھانا کھلایا تو گویا کہ اس نے کھانا ان کے لئے مباح کر دیا اور اباحت میں بھی چونکہ اطعام کا معنی پایا جاتا ہے، لہذا کفارہ ظہار ادا ہو جائے گا۔ درحقیقت یہ اصول امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کے خلاف حجت ہے، کیونکہ امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ اطعام کو زکوۃ اور صدقہ فطر پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ تم ایک ضروری ہے۔ جبکہ احناف کہتے ہیں کہ کفارہ ظہار میں قرآن کریم میں فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّيْنَ مِسْكِيْنًا آیا ہے، اور اطعام کے حقیقی معنی ہیں طعام پر قدرت دینا۔
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب الظهار، فصل فى الكفارة، ج ۲ ص ۴۲۱، ط: رحمانيه
فإن غـداهـم وعشاهم جاز، قليلا كتان منا أكلوا أو كثيراً) لأن المنصوص عليه هو الإطعام، وهو حقيقة فى التمكين من الطعم، وفى الإباحة ذلك كما في التملیک، بخلاف الواجب فى الزكاة وصدقة الفطر، فإنه الإيتاء والأداء ، وهما للتمليك حقيقة.
اللباب في شرح الكتاب: كتاب الظهار، ج ۳ ص ۷۳، ط: المكتبة العلمية
Feeding (it'am) in its literal sense is enabling access to food. Translation: The real meaning of it'am is giving power over food. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that it'am in reality refers to giving power over food, i.e., when a person gives another power over food, the meaning of it'am is established. This meaning (giving power over food) is also found in ibaha (making permissible). The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a person who made zihar feeds sixty poor people morning and evening, the expiation is fulfilled, because the meaning of it'am is giving power over food, and when the muzahir (person who made zihar) fed the poor, it is as if he made the food permissible for them, and since the meaning of it'am is found in ibaha, therefore the expiation of zihar is fulfilled. In fact, this principle is an argument against Imam al-Shafi'i, because Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes it'am to zakat and fitr sadaqah, saying that tamlik (transfer of ownership) is necessary. While the Hanafis say that in the expiation of zihar, the Quran says 'feeding sixty poor people' (fa it'amu sittina miskinan), and the real meaning of it'am is giving power over food. Al-Hidayah, Book of Divorce, Chapter of Zihar, Section on Expiation, vol. 2 p. 421, Rahmaniyya edition: For if he feeds them morning and evening, it is valid, whether they eat little or much) Because what is prescribed is it'am, and it is literal in enabling access to food, and that is also in ibaha just as in tamlik, unlike the obligation in zakat and fitr sadaqah, for that is ita' (giving) and ada' (paying), and both are literally for tamlik. Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, Book of Zihar, vol. 3 p. 73, al-Ilmiyya Press.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the meaning of 'it'am' (feeding) in the context of zihar expiation. The principle states that the literal meaning of it'am is enabling access to food (tamkin min al-ta'am), not necessarily transferring ownership. The Hanafi position is that when the Qur'an commands 'fa it'amu sittina miskinan' (then feed sixty poor people), it means giving them food to eat, whether by serving meals or by giving them possession. Therefore, if a person who has made zihar feeds the poor morning and evening (ghada wa 'asha), the expiation is valid even if he does not give them ownership of the food. The Hanafis support this by arguing that the same meaning of it'am (enabling access) applies in the concept of ibaha (making permissible). In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes this to zakat and fitr sadaqah, where tamlik (transfer of ownership) is required, and thus argues that it'am in zihar expiation also requires tamlik. The Hanafi response is that the texts for zakat and fitr use words like 'ita' (giving) and 'ada' (paying), which literally imply tamlik, whereas the text for zihar uses 'it'am', which literally means enabling access, not necessarily ownership. The Hidayah quote clarifies that feeding morning and evening is valid, and this is the relied-upon Hanafi position. The reference to Al-Lubab confirms the same.

Key Terms
إِطْعَام (it'am): Feeding; giving food to someone.
تَمْكِين (tamkin): Enabling; giving someone the ability to access something.
تَمْلِيك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership.
إِبَاحَة (ibaha): Making permissible; granting permission to use without ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How do the Hanafis refute the Shafi'i analogy that 'it'am' in zihar expiation requires tamlik like in zakat?
A) By stating that the Quran uses different words for zakat (ita) and zihar (it'am).
B) By saying that zakat and zihar are different types of obligations.
C) By claiming that the Shafi'i position is based on weak hadith.
D) By agreeing with the analogy but making an exception for zihar.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, it'am means enabling access to food (tamkin), not ownership transfer (tamlik), so serving a meal to the poor fulfills zihar expiation.

The Rule of Intention Within One Genus vs. Two Genera
Legal maxim on intention within same or different genera

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim on intention and apply it to distinguish when separate intentions are required for multiple acts of worship or expiation.

Core Idea
Intention distinguishes between genera; within one genus it is superfluous.

This lesson introduces a foundational maxim from Hanafi fiqh: intention (niyya) is legally irrelevant when performing multiple acts of the same type, but essential when the acts belong to different categories. The principle appears in the Hidayah within the context of zihar expiation, but applies broadly to any situation where multiple obligations or supererogatory acts are performed simultaneously. Understanding this maxim prevents unnecessary complexity in ritual acts.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the Arabic maxim
Commit to memory: 'إِنَّ النِّيَّةَ فِى الْجِنْسِ الْوَاحِدِ لَغْوٌ وَفِى الْجِنْسَيْنِ مُعْتَبَرَةٌ'. This is a concise rule that you will apply throughout your study of Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand the key terms
Define 'jins' (genus) as a category of acts (e.g., all types of charity, all types of prayers) and 'laghw' as having no legal effect. Recognize that 'niyya' is the internal intention that differentiates between legal categories.
The same genus does not require separate intentions; different genera do.
3
Identify the genus of the acts
Look at the acts you are performing. Are they all the same type (e.g., all are fard prayers, all are zakat payments) or are they of different types (e.g., one fard and one sunnah)?
If uncertain, ask: what is the essential nature of each act?
4
Apply the maxim
If the acts are of the same genus, a single intention suffices, and specifying separate intentions for each act is laghw. If they are of different genera, you must have a distinct intention for each to differentiate them.
Example: Feeding two poor people for the same kaffara requires only one overall intention.
5
Reflect on the wisdom
The maxim prevents unnecessary burden and confusion. Intention's purpose is to distinguish legal categories, not to multiply within a single category.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of ease in worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ النِّيَّةَ فِى الْجِنْسِ الْوَاحِدِ لَغْوٌ وَفِى الْجِنْسَيْنِ مُعْتَبَرَةٌ.
ترجمہ: ایک جنس میں نیت لغو ہو جاتی ہے اور دوجنسوں میں نیت معتبر ہوگی۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایک جنس کی دو چیزوں میں الگ الگ نیت کرنا درست نہیں ہے بلکہ نیت لغو ہوگی، اس لئے کہ نیت اجناس کے درمیان تمییز کے لئے ہوتی ہے،
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب الظهار، فصل فى الكفارة، ج ۲ ص ۴۲۲، ط: رحمانیه
Indeed, intention within the same genus is invalid (laghw), and between two genera it is considered (mu'tabara). Translation: In one genus, intention becomes void, and in two genera, intention will be considered. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that it is not correct to have separate intentions for two things of the same genus; rather, the intention will be void, because intention is for distinguishing between genera. Al-Hidayah, Book of Divorce, Chapter of Zihar, Section on Expiation, vol. 2 p. 422, Rahmaniyya edition.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement of a legal maxim (qa'ida) from the Hidayah concerning the role of intention (niyya) when performing multiple acts of the same kind or different kinds. The principle states that if a person performs multiple acts that are of the same genus (jins wahid) – for example, giving charity to two poor people using the same type of food – then specifying a separate intention for each recipient is superfluous (laghw) because the acts are identical in nature. Intention is needed only to differentiate between different types of acts (jinsayn). For example, if one intends to give both zakat and an ordinary gift, the intention distinguishes them. But if all acts are of the same category (e.g., all are zakat), separate intentions are unnecessary and do not affect the validity. The context in the Hidayah is likely within the chapter on zihar expiation, but the principle is general. The commentary explains that intention serves to distinguish between different genera; hence when the genus is the same, intention has no effect. This maxim is used by Hanafi jurists to resolve cases where multiple identical obligations are performed simultaneously.

Key Terms
نِيَّة (niyya): Intention; the internal purpose behind an act of worship or transaction.
جِنْس (jins): Genus; a category or type of thing. Here refers to the type of act or item.
لَغْو (laghw): Invalid; void; having no effect.
مُعْتَبَر (mu'tabar): Considered; having legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi maxim, what happens if a person feeds two poor people with the same intention of zihar expiation but then tries to make separate intentions for each?
A) Both intentions are valid and required.
B) The intentions are irrelevant because they are of the same genus.
C) Only the first intention is valid.
D) The expiation becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Intention distinguishes between different types of acts, not between identical ones; within the same genus, intention has no legal effect.

The Legal Nature of Li'an: Testimonies Strengthened by Oaths
Defining li'an as testimonies strengthened by oaths, with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of li'an and identify the Quranic proof that establishes it as testimonies strengthened by oaths.

Core Idea
Li'an is testimonies strengthened by oaths, substituting for hadd punishments.

This passage from Al-Hidayah defines the legal nature of li'an (mutual cursing) when a husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses. The Hanafi school emphasizes that li'an is fundamentally a set of testimonies (shahadat) reinforced by oaths (ayman), not merely a divorce procedure. The definition is drawn from the Quranic verses that refer to the husband as a 'witness' and his statements as 'testimonies'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Legal Nature
State that li'an is defined as 'shahadat mu'akkadat bi al-ayman' (testimonies strengthened by oaths). Note that it is connected to cursing (la'n) and substitutes for two hadd punishments: for the husband (hadd al-qadhf) and for the wife (hadd al-zina).
The Arabic term 'شهادات' is plural of 'شهادة', emphasizing the testimony component.
2
Locate the Quranic Proof
Identify the dalil from Surah al-Nur (24:6-7): 'And they have no witnesses except themselves... and the testimony of each of them is four testimonies by Allah.' This is the direct evidence for the definition.
The verse uses both 'شهداء' (witnesses) and 'شهادات' (testimonies), which are the basis of the Hanafi position.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Analyze how the Quranic text proves that li'an consists of testimonies and oaths. The term 'شهادات' indicates testimony, and 'بالله' indicates the oath. The exclusion of other witnesses (except themselves) places the husband in the category of witnesses.
The Hanafi school argues that the primary element is testimony, strengthened by oath, not the opposite.
4
Note the Substitution Effect
Understand that li'an replaces the fixed punishments: for the husband, it substitutes for hadd al-qadhf (80 lashes for false accusation); for the wife, it substitutes for hadd al-zina (stoning or lashes) if she responds with counter-oaths.
This substitution is the practical purpose of li'an.
5
Compare with Other Views (Optional)
Recognize that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) emphasize the oath element more, considering li'an primarily as a set of oaths. The Hanafi view is based on the explicit usage of 'shahadah' in the text.
This difference in definition does not change the outer procedure but reflects differing usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب اللعان
(۱۰۱) الْأَصْلُ أَنَّ اللَّعَانَ عِنْدَنَا شَهَادَاتٌ مُؤَكَّدَاتٌ بِالْأَيْمَانِ مَقْرُوْنَةٌ بِاللَّعْنِ قَائِمَةٌ مَقَامَ حَدِ الْقَذَفِ فِى حَقِهِ وَمَقَامَ حَدِ الزِّنَا فِي حَقِّهَا .
الهداية: كتاب الطلاق، باب اللعان ج ۲ ص ۴۲۳، ط: رحمانيه لأنَّ اللَّعَانَ عِنْدَنَا شَهَادَاتٌ مُوَكَّدَاتٌ بِالْأَيْمَانِ مَقْرُونَةٌ بِاللَّعْنِ قَائِمَةٌ مَقَامَ حَدٌ الْقَذْفِ فِي حَقِّهِ وَمَقَامَ حَدٌ الزِّنَا فِي حَقَّهَا لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَلَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُمْ شُهَدَاء إِلا أَنْفُسُهُمْ) فَسَمَّاهُمْ شُهَدَاءَ وَاسْتَكْنَاهُمْ مِنْ جُمْلَةِ الشُّهَدَاءِ وَالِاسْتِثْنَاءِ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ مِنْ الْجِنْسِ وَقَالَ تَعَالَى (فَشَهَادَةُ أَحَدِهِمُ أَرْبَعُ شَهَادَاتٍ بِاللَّهِ نَضٌ عَلَى الشَّهَادَةِ وَالْيَمِينِ فَقُلْنَا الرُّكْنُ هُوَ الشَّهَادَةُ الْمُؤَكَّدَةُ بِالْيَمِينِ ثُمَّ قَرَنَ الرُّكْنَ فِى جَانِبِهِ بِاللَّعْن لَوْ كَانَ كَاذِبًا وَهُوَ قَائِمٌ مَقَامَ حَدٌ الْقَذْفِ وَفِي جَانِبِهَا بِالْغَضَبِ وَهُوَ قَائِمٌ مَقَامَ حَدٌ الزَّنَا.
الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب اللعان، ج ۲ ص ۷۳، ط: المطبعة الخيرية
Chapter of Li'an. (101) The principle is that li'an with us is testimonies strengthened by oaths, connected with cursing, standing in place of the hadd of qadhf in his right and in place of the hadd of zina in her right. Al-Hidayah... because li'an with us is testimonies strengthened by oaths, connected with cursing, standing in place of the hadd of qadhf in his right and in place of the hadd of zina in her right, due to His statement the Most High: 'And they have no witnesses except themselves,' so He called them witnesses and classified them among the category of witnesses, and exclusion is only from the genus. And He said the Most High: 'And the testimony of each of them is four testimonies by Allah,' which is explicit regarding testimony and oath. So we said the pillar is the testimony strengthened by the oath. Then He connected the pillar in his side with cursing if he is lying, and it stands in place of the hadd of qadhf, and in her side with wrath, and it stands in place of the hadd of zina.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage defines the legal nature of li'an (mutual cursing between spouses) according to the Hanafi school. The author states the principle that li'an is essentially a set of testimonies (shahadat) that are strengthened by oaths (ayman) and linked to the invocation of curse (la'n). These testimonies function as a substitute for the hadd punishment: for the husband, li'an replaces the hadd for false accusation of adultery (qadhf), and for the wife, it replaces the hadd for adultery (zina). This definition is supported by a dalil from the Quran (Surah al-Nur, verse 6-7), where Allah refers to the husband as a 'witness' and describes his four oaths as 'shahadat' (testimonies). The Hanafi scholars conclude that the pillar of li'an is the testimony strengthened by oath, and the curse and wrath are attached as consequences. The Jawhara al-Nayyira is referenced for further detail.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li'an): A mutual process of swearing oaths between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of adultery without witnesses, including curse and wrath.
شهادات مؤكدات بالأيمان (shahadat mu'akkadat bi al-ayman): Testimonies that are reinforced with oaths, forming the core of li'an.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment for false accusation of adultery, which is 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle, what does li'an substitute for the husband?
A) Hadd al-zina
B) Hadd al-qadhf
C) The penalty for perjury
D) The obligation of divorce

Key Takeaway
Li'an is legally defined as testimonies strengthened by oaths, substituting for hadd punishments, as established by the Quranic wording in Surah al-Nur.

Li'an Ruling Ceases After Husband's Self-Retraction
Ruling that li'an effects terminate upon retraction, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of the husband's retraction (ikdhab) in li'an and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding remarriage.

Core Idea
Retraction of li'an accusation nullifies the li'an ruling; the husband may remarry, but a conflicting narration forbids it.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a key principle: the legal effects of li'an do not persist after the husband admits his accusation was false. Within the Hanafi school, there is a disagreement about whether the couple can remarry. We will examine the evidence and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
The passage rules that after the husband retracts his li'an accusation (ikdhab) and is flogged, he may remarry his former wife. This is the view of the Sahibayn.
The ruling applies only after retraction, not if the husband persists.
2
Understand the opposing narration
Abu Yusuf has a conflicting narration that prohibits remarriage, citing the hadith 'The two who curse each other will never be together forever.'
This shows an intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Sahibayn argue that retraction is a withdrawal of testimony; testimony after withdrawal has no effect. Therefore li'an is nullified, as evidenced by the implementation of the hadd and establishment of lineage, both incompatible with li'an.
The hadd and lineage are indicators that the li'an status has ended.
4
Interpret the hadith
The hadith is interpreted conditionally: the prohibition applies only as long as the couple remain li'an participants. After retraction, the husband ceases to be a li'an participant both literally and metaphorically.
This interpretation is supported by similar conditional phrases in the Qur'an and common speech.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn: the husband may remarry.
Al-Hidayah states 'وَهَذَا عِنْدَهُمَا' indicating this is the preferred view.

Source Text

( ١٠٢ ) إِنَّ حُكْمَ التَّلَاعُنِ لَا يَبْقَى بَعْدَ الْإِكْذَابِ .
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب اللعان، ج ۲ ص ۴۲، ط: رحمانیه (وَلَهُ أَنْ يَنْكِحَهَا) أَى لَهُ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ بِهَا بَعْدَمَا أَكْذَبَ نَفْسَهُ، وَحُدَّ وَهَذَا عِنْدَهُمَا، وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَيْسَ لَهُ ذَلِكَ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ الْمُتَلاعِنَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ أَبَدًا رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُد بِمَعْنَاهُ، وَمِثْلُهُ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ وَابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ وَابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَوَاهُ الدَّارَقُطْنِي، وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ الْإِكْذَابَ رُجُوعٌ، وَالشَّهَادَةَ بَعْدِ الرُّجُوعِ لَا حُكْمَ لَهَا فِي حَقِّ الرَّاجِعِ فَيَرْتَفِعُ اللَّعَانُ، وَلِهَذَا يُحَدُّ، وَيَثْبُتُ نَسَبُ الوَلَدِ، وَلَا يَجْتَمِعُ الحَدُّ وَاللَّعَانُ فَلَزِمَ مِنْ إِقَامَةِ الْحَدَّ الْتِفَاء اللَّعَانِ، وَكَذَا لَا يَنْفِى اللَّعَانَ مَعَ ثبوتِ النَّسَبِ وَمَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ الْمُتَلاعِنَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ أَبَدًا أَى مَا دَامَا مُتَلَاعِنَيْنِ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَلَا تُصَلِّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْهُمْ مَاتَ أَبَدًا أَى مَا دَامَ مُنَافِقًا يُقَالُ الْمُصَلَّى لَا يَتَكَلَّمُ أَيْ مَا دَامَ مُصَلِّيًا فَلَمْ يَبْقَ مُتَلَاعِنَا لَا حَقِيقَةً لِعَدَمِ الاشْتِغَالِ بِهِ، وَلَا مَجَازًا لِأَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا سُمِّيَ مُتَلَاعَنا لِبَقَاءِ اللعان بَيْنَهُمَا حُكْمًا، وَلَمْ يَبْقَ .
تبيين الحقائق: كتاب اللعان، ج ۳ ص ۱۹، ط: المطبعة الكبرى الأميرية
(102) Indeed, the ruling of li'an does not remain after retraction. Al-Hidayah: (And he may marry her) i.e., he may marry her after he has retracted his statement and been flogged. And this is according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf said: He does not have that, because of the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The two who curse each other will never be together forever,' reported by Abu Dawud with its meaning, and similar from Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Abbas, reported by al-Daraqutni. And for both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that retraction is a withdrawal, and testimony after withdrawal has no ruling in the right of the one withdrawing, so li'an is lifted. For this reason he is flogged, and the lineage of the child is established, and the hadd and li'an do not combine. So it follows from implementing the hadd that li'an is eliminated. Similarly, li'an does not negate lineage when established. And the meaning of his statement 'the two who curse each other will never be together forever' is as long as they are li'an participants, like His statement: 'And do not ever pray over any of them who dies' i.e., as long as he is a hypocrite. One says 'the one praying does not speak' i.e., as long as he is praying. So he does not remain a li'an participant, neither in reality due to not engaging in it, nor metaphorically because he was only called a li'an participant for the survival of li'an between them as a ruling, and it did not remain.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage presents the principle that the legal effects of li'an (i.e., permanent separation) do not continue after the husband retracts his accusation (ikdhab). The commentary from Al-Hidayah clarifies: after the husband retracts his own accusation (by admitting he lied), he is flogged for qadhf, and he may remarry his former wife. This is the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). However, a different transmission from Abu Yusuf states that he may not remarry, citing the hadith that 'the two who curse each other will never be together forever.' The Sahibayn's reasoning is that retraction is a withdrawal of the testimony; testimony after withdrawal has no legal effect in the right of the one who withdrew, so li'an is nullified. This is supported by the fact that the hadd is carried out and lineage is established, both of which are incompatible with the continuation of li'an. The hadith is interpreted conditionally: the prohibition of reunion applies only as long as both remain in the state of li'an participants; once the husband retracts, he is no longer a li'an participant. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq is referenced for further detail.

Key Terms
الإكذاب (al-ikdhab): The husband's retraction of his li'an accusation, admitting he lied.
المتلاعنان (al-mutala'inan): The two spouses who have performed li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the result of the husband retracting his li'an accusation according to the Sahibayn?
A) Li'an remains in effect, and they cannot remarry
B) Li'an is nullified, and he may remarry
C) The wife must perform additional oaths
D) The marriage is automatically renewed

Key Takeaway
Retraction (ikdhab) of the husband in li'an nullifies the li'an ruling, and according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, he may remarry his former wife.

Effect of Retraction (Ikdhab) After Li'an
States principle and intra-Hanafi dispute on li'an after retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the effect of the husband's retraction after li'an on the permanent prohibition and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding remarriage.

Core Idea
The husband's retraction (ikdhab) after li'an lifts the permanent prohibition, allowing remarriage, but Abu Yusuf dissents based on a hadith.

This lesson examines a key principle from Usool-e-Hidayah: the ruling of li'an does not persist after the husband retracts his accusation. The passage presents the operative position (mufta bihi) that the husband may remarry his ex-wife after being punished for qadhf, but also records a nuanced intra-madhhab disagreement with Abu Yusuf. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh evidence and apply tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Read the principle (102): 'The ruling of li'an does not remain after retraction.' Identify the specific ruling of li'an being referred to (permanent prohibition of marriage).
The principle is a concise legal maxim that guides subsequent rulings.
2
Identify the Dispute and Parties
Note that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that retraction nullifies li'an, allowing remarriage. Abu Yusuf opposes this view.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; all three are founders of the school.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's Proof
Abu Yusuf cites the hadith: 'The two who engage in li'an will never be together forever.' Identify the source (Abu Dawud, al-Daraqutni) and its apparent literal meaning.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The majority Hanafis interpret the hadith as conditional: 'as long as they remain mutala'in.' They draw parallels from the Qur'an (9:84) and everyday usage (e.g., 'the one praying does not speak'). Retraction ends the state of li'an, so the prohibition ceases.
Other supporting arguments: hadd and li'an cannot coexist; lineage is established; testimony after revocation has no effect.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. Conclude that after retraction and hadd punishment, the husband may remarry his ex-wife.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

( ١٠٢ ) إِنَّ حُكْمَ التَّلَاعُنِ لَا يَبْقَى بَعْدَ الْإِكْذَابِ .
ترجمہ: بے شک لعان کا حکم جھٹلانے کے بعد باقی نہیں رہتا۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ لعان کا حکم یعنی زوجین میں فرقت کے بعد حرمت ابدی کا ہونا، یہ جھٹلانے کے بعد ثابت نہیں ہوگی، یعنی اگر شوہر نے اپنے آپ کو جھٹلا دیا تو شوہر پر حد قذف جاری ہوگی اور اب اس کے لئے سابقہ بیوی سے نکاح جائز ہے کیونکہ لعان میں یہ شرط تھی کہ میاں بیوی اہل شہادت میں سے ہوں لیکن بعد میں جب شوہر پر حد جاری ہوئی ہو تو یہ اہل شہادت نہ رہا، اہلیت ختم ہو گئی، جب اہلیت ختم ہوئی تو حکم بھی ختم ہو گیا، لہذا ان کے درمیان جو لعان ہوا تھا وہ کالعدم شمار ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں شوہر نے لعان کے بعد دوبارہ اعادہ کیا اور اپنی تکذیب کی تو قاضی اس پر حد قذف جاری کرے گا اور اب اس شوہر کے لئے اپنے آپ کو جھٹلانے کے بعد لعان کا حکم یعنی حرمت ابدی باقی نہ رہے گی، جب حرمت باقی نہ رہی تو اب نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب اللعان، ج ۲ ص ۴۲، ط: رحمانيه (وَلَهُ أَنْ يَنْكِحَهَا) أَى لَهُ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ بِهَا بَعْدَمَا أَكْذَبَ نَفْسَهُ، وَحُدَّ وَهَذَا عِنْدَهُمَا، وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَيْسَ لَهُ ذَلِكَ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ الْمُتَلاعِنَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ أَبَدًا رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُد بِمَعْنَاهُ، وَمِثْلُهُ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ وَابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ وَابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَوَاهُ الدَّارَقُطْنِي، وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ الْإِكْذَابَ رُجُوعٌ، وَالشَّهَادَةَ بَعْدِ الرُّجُوعِ لَا حُكْمَ لَهَا فِي حَقِّ الرَّاجِعِ فَيَرْتَفِعُ اللَّعَانُ، وَلِهَذَا يُحَدُّ، وَيَثْبُتُ نَسَبُ الوَلَدِ، وَلَا يَجْتَمِعُ الحَدُّ وَاللَّعَانُ فَلَزِمَ مِنْ إِقَامَةِ الْحَدَّ الْتِفَاء اللَّعَانِ، وَكَذَا لَا يَنْفِى اللَّعَانَ مَعَ ثبوتِ النَّسَبِ وَمَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ الْمُتَلاعِنَانِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ أَبَدًا أَى مَا دَامَا مُتَلَاعِنَيْنِ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَلَا تُصَلِّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْهُمْ مَاتَ أَبَدًا أَى مَا دَامَ مُنَافِقًا يُقَالُ الْمُصَلَّى لَا يَتَكَلَّمُ أَيْ مَا دَامَ مُصَلِّيًا فَلَمْ يَبْقَ مُتَلاعِنَا لَا حَقِيقَةً لِعَدَمِ الاشْتِغَالِ بِهِ، وَلَا مَجَازًا لِأَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا سُمِّيَ مُتَلاعَنا لِبَقَاءِ اللعان بَيْنَهُمَا حُكْمًا، وَلَمْ يَبْقَ .
تبيين الحقائق: كتاب اللعان، ج ۳ ص ۱۹، ط: المطبعة الكبرى الأميرية
The ruling of li'an does not remain after retraction. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that the ruling of li'an, i.e., permanent prohibition after separation between spouses, is not established after retraction. That is, if the husband disavows himself, the hadd of qadhf will be imposed on him, and then marriage to his former wife is permissible for him, because li'an had the condition that the spouses be among those qualified for testimony, but after hadd is imposed, he is no longer qualified. His qualification is gone, and when qualification is gone, the ruling is also gone. Therefore, the li'an that occurred between them will be considered void. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if the husband repeats his accusation after li'an and then retracts, the judge will impose hadd of qadhf on him, and after retraction, the ruling of li'an, i.e., permanent prohibition, will not remain. When prohibition does not remain, marriage is permissible. Al-Hidayah, Book of Divorce, Chapter of Li'an, vol. 2, p. 42, Rahmaniyya ed: (And he may marry her) i.e., he may marry her after he disavows himself and is punished with hadd. This is their view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: He does not have that right because of the Prophet's statement: 'The two who engage in li'an will never be together forever' – Abu Dawud narrated it with similar meaning. Similar is reported from Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Abbas – narrated by al-Daraqutni. Their evidence (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) is that retraction is a revocation, and testimony after revocation has no effect in the revoker's right, so li'an is lifted. For this reason, hadd is imposed, and lineage of the child is established. Hadd and li'an cannot coexist, so imposing hadd necessitates lifting li'an. Similarly, li'an cannot negate lineage once established. And the meaning of his statement 'the two who engage in li'an will never be together forever' is as long as they are engaged in li'an, like His statement: 'And never pray for any of them who dies' (9:84) meaning as long as he is a hypocrite. It is said: 'The one praying does not speak' meaning as long as he is praying. So he is not mutala'in, neither literally because he is not engaged in it, nor metaphorically because he was only called mutala'in due to the legal persistence of li'an between them, and it no longer persists.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage presents a key principle (102) from Usool-e-Hidayah regarding the legal effect of a husband's retraction after li'an. The author begins by stating the principle: the ruling of li'an does not remain after the husband's retraction (ikdhab). The Urdu commentary clarifies that the specific ruling of li'an—permanent prohibition of marriage between the spouses—ceases when the husband admits he lied. The author explains the reasoning: li'an requires the spouses to be qualified witnesses; after the husband is punished for qadhf, he loses that qualification, thus the li'an becomes void. The source text from Al-Hidayah then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (often called 'Sahibayn'), the husband may remarry his ex-wife after retraction and punishment. Abu Yusuf, however, opposes, citing a hadith that those who engage in li'an can never be reunited. The Hanafi response (of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) interprets the hadith as meaning 'as long as they remain in the state of li'an' – which ends with retraction. They also argue that hadd and li'an cannot coexist, and once hadd is imposed, li'an is lifted. The commentary emphasizes that the correct position (mufta bihi) is that the husband can remarry after retraction.

Key Terms
التلَاعُن (al-tala'un): Mutual imprecation; the process of li'an between spouses.
الإكْذَاب (al-ikdhab): Retraction or disavowal; the husband admitting he lied in his accusation.
حرمة أبدية (hurmat abadiyyah): Permanent prohibition of marriage between the spouses after a complete li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle (102) and the Hanafi position, what happens if a husband retracts his accusation after li'an?
A) The marriage remains permanently prohibited.
B) The husband is punished with hadd of qadhf and may remarry his wife.
C) The li'an is confirmed and the separation is permanent.
D) The wife is punished for zina.

Key Takeaway
The retraction (ikdhab) of the husband after li'an nullifies the permanent prohibition of marriage, per the majority of Hanafi imams, because hadd and li'an cannot coexist and the hadith is interpreted conditionally.

Li'an Requires Explicit Accusation Not Gestures
States principle and inter-madhhab dispute on validity of li'an by gestures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that li'an requires explicit speech and explain why gestures of a deaf-mute are insufficient, using the analogy to hadd penalties.

Core Idea
Li'an requires explicit verbal accusation; gestures are invalid because li'an replaces hadd, and doubt averts hadd.

Li'an (mutual curse) is a serious process that substitutes for the fixed punishment (hadd) of qadhf (false accusation of adultery). Because it carries such weight, Hanafi jurists require the utmost clarity and explicitness. This lesson examines the principle that li'an must be initiated with explicit speech (sarih) and applies it to the case of a deaf-mute (akhras) who can only gesture. We will explore the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and contrast it with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: li'an is not established by gestures; only explicit verbal accusation suffices. The deaf-mute's gesture does not count.
Principle: 'Li'an is attached to explicit speech.'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a deaf-mute's gesture is equivalent to explicit speech, so li'an can be performed by gesture.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argument: Gestures of a deaf-mute are legally treated as explicit speech in all contexts, based on necessity and analogy.
The opponent's dalil is i'tibar of gesture as speech.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafi rebuttal: (1) Li'an stands in place of hadd; hadd is averted by doubts. Gestures inherently involve doubt. (2) Li'an requires the specific wording 'ashhadu' (I testify). Gestures cannot fulfill this requirement.
Two independent reasons; either suffices to invalidate.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafis rule that a deaf-mute husband cannot perform li'an at all. Shafi'is allow it. If the wife is deaf-mute, Hanafis also rule no li'an because she cannot utter the required testimony, whereas Shafi'is may allow by gesture.
The difference affects the legal status of the marriage and paternity.

Source Text

(۱۰۳) إِنَّ اللَّعَانَ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالصَّرِيحِ .
ترجمہ: لعان صراحت کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ لعان اس وقت ثابت ہو گا جب شوہر بیوی پر تہمت کی صراحت کرے یعنی زبان سے صراحتاً اس پر زنا کی تہمت لگائے یا بچے کی نفی کرے، لہذا اشارے سے لعان ثابت نہ ہوگا، اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لعان حد کے قائم مقام ہے اور حد و د صراحت
سے ثابت ہوتے ہیں اور شبہ سے ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں، لہذ العان میں بھی صراحت ضروری ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر گونگا آدمی اپنی بیوی پر اشارے سے تہمت لگائے تو لعان ثابت نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ لعان کا تعلق صراحتاً تہمت سے ہے اور گونگے کی تہمت صراحتاً نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اشارے سے ہوتی ہے، لہذا گونگے کی تہمت سے لعان نہیں ہوگا۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس کے اشارے میں شبہ ہے اور لعان حد کے قائم مقام ہے اور حدود شبہات سے ساقط ہو جاتی ہیں لہذا العان بھی شبہ کی وجہ سے ساقط ہوگا۔
الهداية: كتاب الطلاق باب اللعان ج ۲ ص ۴۲۵، ط: رحمانیه
(وَلَا لِعَانَ بِقَدْفِ الْأَخْرَسِ)، وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَجِبُ اللَّعَانُ بِهِ لِأَنَّ إِشَارَتَهُ كَالصَّرِيحِ، وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ قَائِمٌ مَقَامَ حَدَّ الْقَذْفِ فِي حَقِّهِ، وَقَذَفَهُ لَا يَعْرَى عَنْ شُبُهَةٍ، وَالْحُدُودُ تُدْرَأُ بِهَا، وَلَأَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ مِنْ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِلَفْظِ الشَّهَادَةِ فِي اللَّعَانِ حَتَّى لَوْ قَالَ أَحْلِفُ مَكَانَ أَشْهَدُ لَا يَجُوزُ، وَإِشَارَتُهُ لَا تَكُونُ شَهَادَةً، وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا كَانَتْ هِيَ خَرْسَاء لِأَنَّ قَذْفَهَا لَا يُوجِبُ الْحَدَّ لِاحْتِمَالِ أَنَّهَا تُصَدِّقُهُ أَوْ لِتَعَذَّرِ الْإِلْيَان بِلَفْظِ الشَّهَادَةِ.
تبيين الحقائق: كتاب اللعان، ج ۳ ص ۲۰، ط: المطبعة الكبرى الأميرية
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب اللعان ج ۲ ص ۴۲۵، ط: رحمانیه
(103) Indeed, li'an is attached to explicit (speech). Translation: Li'an is attached to explicitness. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that li'an will be established only when the husband makes an explicit accusation against his wife, i.e., explicitly accuses her of adultery with his tongue or negates the child. Therefore, li'an is not established by gestures. The reason is that li'an stands in place of hadd (punishment), and hadd penalties are established by explicitness and are dropped due to doubt. So in li'an, explicitness is also necessary. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a deaf-mute man accuses his wife by gesture, li'an will not be established, because li'an is attached to explicit accusation, and a deaf-mute's accusation is not explicit but by gesture. Therefore, li'an does not occur from a deaf-mute's accusation. The second reason is that his gesture involves doubt, and li'an stands in place of hadd, and hadd penalties are dropped due to doubts, so li'an also drops due to doubt. Al-Hidayah: Book of Divorce, Chapter of Li'an, vol. 2, p. 425, Rahmaniyya ed: (And there is no li'an with the accusation of a deaf-mute.) Al-Shafi'i said: Li'an is obligatory by it because his gesture is like explicit speech. Our evidence is that it stands in place of the hadd of qadhf in his case, and his accusation is not free from doubt, and hadd penalties are warded off by doubts. Also, it is necessary to utter the wording of testimony in li'an; so if he says 'I swear' instead of 'I testify', it is not permissible, and his gesture does not constitute testimony. Similarly, if the wife is a deaf-mute, because her accusation does not necessitate hadd due to the possibility that she may confirm him, or due to the difficulty of her performing the oath with the wording of testimony. Tabyin al-Haqaiq: Book of Li'an, vol. 3, p. 20, Al-Matba'ah al-Kubra al-Amiriyya ed. Al-Hidayah: Book of Divorce, Chapter of Li'an, vol. 2, p. 425, Rahmaniyya ed.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage presents principle (103) from Usool-e-Hidayah: li'an is only valid with explicit accusation. The Urdu commentary explains that for li'an to be established, the husband must explicitly accuse his wife of adultery or deny paternity. Gestures are insufficient. The reasoning: li'an takes the place of hadd (fixed punishment), and hadd is only applied when there is explicit proof and is dropped due to doubts. Therefore, li'an also requires explicitness. The author then applies this to a deaf-mute (akhras): a deaf-mute's gesture cannot form the basis of li'an because it lacks explicitness and involves doubt. The source text from Al-Hidayah presents an inter-madhhab dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a deaf-mute's gesture is equivalent to explicit speech, so li'an is established. The Hanafi response is that li'an stands in place of hadd, and hadd is averted by doubts; the gesture is doubtful. Moreover, li'an requires the utterance of the word 'ashhadu' (I testify), which gestures cannot fulfill. The same applies if the wife is a deaf-mute: her accusation does not necessitate hadd because she might confirm the accusation or cannot perform the required oath wording.

Key Terms
الصريح (al-sarih): Explicit speech; clear, unambiguous verbal accusation.
الأخرس (al-akhras): A deaf-mute person who cannot speak or hear; communicates by gestures.
الشهادة (al-shahadah): Testimony; in li'an, the husband must say 'ashhadu' (I testify) to initiate the process.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is li'an not established by the gesture of a deaf-mute husband?
A) Because the gesture is not explicit and involves doubt, and hadd penalties are averted by doubts.
B) Because the gesture does not constitute testimony, and li'an requires the specific word 'ashhadu'.
C) Both A and B.
D) Because the deaf-mute is not legally responsible.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a high-stakes procedure that substitutes for hadd; therefore, only explicit verbal accusation suffices, and gestures—especially those of a deaf-mute—are invalid due to doubt and the inability to pronounce the required testimony wording.

Husband Denying Paternity Without Certainty: No Qadhf or Li'an
Intra-Hanafi dispute on li'an when husband denies pregnancy uncertainly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on whether li'an is required when a husband denies paternity without certainty of pregnancy, and apply the principle that qadhf cannot be conditional.

Core Idea
Qadhf cannot be conditional—without certainty of pregnancy, no li'an.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of li'an when a husband says 'laysa hamluk minni' (your pregnancy is not from me) without being certain of pregnancy. Imam Abu Hanifa and Zufar hold that no li'an is required because the husband is not a qadhif at the moment of speech. The Sahibayn argue that if birth occurs within six months, certainty is retroactive, and li'an must be performed. We will examine the proofs and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The husband's statement 'laysa hamluk minni' is a denial of paternity. The dispute is whether this triggers li'an (mutual cursing) or is considered qadhf (false accusation of zina).
2
State the Hanafi majority position (Abu Hanifa and Zufar)
Abu Hanifa and Zufar hold that no li'an is required because at the time of the statement, the husband is not certain that the wife is pregnant, so he is not a qadhif.
3
Present the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that if the wife gives birth within six months, we become certain she was pregnant at the time of the statement, so the husband is a qadhif and li'an is wajib.
The six-month period is the minimum duration of pregnancy in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa responds that the husband's statement is like a conditional (ta'liq): 'If you are pregnant, it is not from me.' Since qadhf cannot be suspended on a condition, the statement is not valid qadhf.
This is an aqli (rational) proof based on the nature of qadhf.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah relies on the view of Abu Hanifa and Zufar, making it the operative position for fatwa. Thus, no li'an in such cases.
Authority: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ وَإِذَا قَالَ الزَّوْجُ لَيْسَ حَمُلُكَ مِنِّى فَلا لِعَانَ هَذَا قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَزُفَرَ، لِأَنَّهُ لَمُ يَتَيَقَّنُ بِقِيَامِ الْحَمْلِ فَلَمْ يَصِرُ قَادِفًا (وَعِنْدَهُمَا إِنْ جَاءَتْ بِهِ لِأَقَلَّ مِنْ سِتَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَهُوَ قَادَتْ وَيُلاعِنُ)، لأنَّا تَيَقَّنَّا وُجُودَهُ عِنْدَ الْقَذْفِ قُلْنَا إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ قَادِفًا فِي الْحَالِ صَارَ كَالْمُعَلَّقِ بِالشَّرْطِ فَكَأَنَّهُ قَالَ إِنْ كَتَانَ بِكَ حَمُلٌ فَلَيْسَ مِنِّى وَالْقَذَفَ لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيقُهُ بِالشَّرْطِ وَإِنْ جَاءَتْ بِهِ لِسِتَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَلَا لِعَانَ، لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَتَيَقَّنُ وُجُودَهُ عِنْدَ الْقَذْفِ فَلَا يُلَاعِنُ بِالشَّكِّ.
His statement: And when the husband says 'Your pregnancy is not from me,' there is no li'an. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Zufar, because he is not certain of the existence of pregnancy, so he does not become a qadhif. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): If she gives birth before six months, then he is a qadhif and they do li'an, because we are certain of its existence at the time of qadhf. We say: Since he is not a qadhif at present, it becomes like something suspended on a condition, as if he said: If there is a pregnancy with you, it is not from me. And qadhf cannot be validly suspended on a condition. And if she gives birth at six months, then there is no li'an, because we are not certain of its existence at the time of qadhf, so he does not do li'an based on doubt.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of li'an (mutual cursing) when a husband denies paternity without certainty of pregnancy. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar hold that no li'an is required because at the time of the statement, the husband is not certain that the wife is pregnant; hence he is not a qadhif (one who accuses of zina). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that if the wife gives birth before six months from the statement, then it is known that she was pregnant at the time, so the husband is considered a qadhif and li'an must be performed. Abu Hanifa responds that this is like suspending qadhf on a condition, which is invalid; thus no li'an even after birth. If she gives birth at six months or later, even the Sahibayn agree no li'an because there is no certainty. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Zufar, as it preserves the principle that qadhf cannot be conditional.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): Falsely accusing a married person of zina, which incurs hadd punishment or li'an.
لعان (li'an): Mutual cursing between spouses when husband accuses wife of zina without witnesses, leading to separation.
تعليق بالشرط (ta'liq bil-shart): Suspending a legal effect on a future condition; here, qadhf cannot be suspended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is there no li'an when a husband says 'laysa hamluk minni' without certainty of pregnancy?
A) Because the wife did not give birth yet.
B) Because the husband's statement is treated as conditional qadhf, which is invalid.
C) Because li'an is only for confirmed zina.
D) Because the husband can simply divorce her.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, qadhf (and consequently li'an) cannot be conditional; without certainty of pregnancy at the time of denial, no li'an is required.
