The Principle of al-Ghalib bi-Manzihat al-Muhaqqaq Applied to a Woman Using Oil During Iddah
Explaining the principle of al-ghalib bi-manzilat al-muhaqqaq and its application to oil use during iddah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of al-ghalib bi-manzilat al-muhaqqaq and apply it to determine the permissibility of a woman in iddah using oil for fear of harm.

Core Idea
The dominant conjecture of harm is treated as actual harm, permitting oil use during iddah.

This passage from al-Hidayah demonstrates a key Hanafi tool of istihsan: the principle that the dominant (al-ghālib) is like the certain (al-muḥaqqaq). The author applies it to the case of a woman in iddah who fears headache if she does not apply oil. The ruling is that it is permissible, provided she does not intend adornment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
What is the ruling on a woman in iddah applying oil? Is it absolutely prohibited or permitted under certain conditions?
The general principle is that a woman in iddah should avoid adornment; oil might be considered adornment.
2
State the Hanafi principle
The principle 'al-ghālib bi-manzilat al-muḥaqqaq' means the dominant (in conjecture) is treated as certain. This is a tool of istihsan to relax strict rulings when there is a strong probability of harm.
This is not a textual proof (naqli) but a rational principle (aqli) derived from legal reasoning.
3
Apply the principle to the scenario
If a woman has a dominant fear (ghalib) that she will suffer headache or eye pain without oil, that fear is treated as actual harm. Hence, necessity is established, making the use of oil permissible.
The dominant fear must be based on custom (ʿādah) or medical advice, not mere whim.
4
Note the condition
The permission is conditional: she must not intend adornment (zīnah). The oil is used solely for treatment or prevention of harm.
If she uses it for beautification, it would be prohibited.
5
Identify the authority
The ruling is from al-Hidayah (Zahir al-Riwayah) and supported by al-Muhit al-Burhani, indicating its weight in the Hanafi school.
Zahir al-Riwayah texts are the most authoritative transmissions of Imam Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو شے غالب ہو وہ اس شے کی مانند ہوتی ہے جو شے واقع اور ثابت ہو لہذا اس غالب الوجود شے پر وہی حکم مرتب ہوگا جونفس الامر میں واقع اور ثابت ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر معدہ عورت تیل استعمال کرنے کی عادی تھی اب اگر اس کو اس بات کا قوی اندیشہ ہو کہ اگر تیل استعمال نہیں کرے گی تو سر میں در داور تکلیف ہوگی تو اس صورت میں اس کے لئے تیل لگانا جائز ہے، کیونکہ جب در دسر کا غالب گمان ہے اور غالب واقع کی مانند ہے، لہذ اغالب کو واقع کا درجہ دیا جائے گا اور اس کے لئے تیل لگانا جائز ہوگا۔
أما في حالة الاضطرار فلا بأس بها بأن اشتكت رأسها أو عينها فصبت عليه الدهن، أو أكتحلت لأجل المعالجة فلا بأس ولكن لا تقصد به الزينة، وكذلك إن اعتادت الدهن فخافت وجعاً يحل بها لو لم تفعل فلا بأس به إذا كان الغالب هذا الحلول، لأن الضرر الذى يلحق غالباً بمنزلة المتحقق فيجب الاحتراز عنه لكن لا تقصد به الزينة لما قلنا. المحيط البرهاني كتاب الطلاق، الفصل الثاني والعشرون، ج ۳ ص ۴۷۰، ط: دار الكتب العلمية الهداية: كتاب الطلاق، باب العدة، فصل ج ۲ ص ۴۳۳، ط: رحمانیه
The meaning of the mentioned principle is that the thing which is dominant is like the thing which is actual and established. Therefore, on this dominantly existing thing, the same ruling will apply as is actual and established in reality. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning the above principle, is explaining that if a woman in iddah was accustomed to using oil, and now she has a strong fear that if she does not use oil, she will get a headache or pain, then in this case it is permissible for her to apply oil, because the dominant conjecture of pain [exists], and the dominant is like the actual. Therefore, the dominant will be given the status of the actual, and it will be permissible for her to apply oil. As for a case of necessity, there is no harm: if she complains of her head or eye and pours oil on it, or applies kohl for treatment, there is no harm, but she should not intend adornment. Similarly, if she was accustomed to oil and fears pain that would befall her if she did not do it, there is no harm if this occurrence is dominant, because harm that attaches predominantly is like the confirmed, so it is necessary to guard against it, but she should not intend adornment due to what we said. [From al-Muhit al-Burhani, Book of Divorce, Chapter 22, vol. 3 p. 470, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah; al-Hidayah: Book of Divorce, Chapter of Iddah, section, vol. 2 p. 433, Rahmaniyyah]
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage demonstrates the Hanafi principle of al-ghalib bi-manzilat al-muhaqqaq, a tool of istihsan. The ruling is that a woman in iddah may apply oil for medical necessity even though it involves adornment-like acts, because the dominant fear of harm makes the necessity real. The principle is applied to permit what would otherwise be discouraged. The source texts are from al-Muhit al-Burhani and al-Hidayah (Zahir al-Riwayah). The teacher should explain that the Hanafi school uses this principle to relax strict rulings when dominant conjecture of harm exists.

Key Terms
الغالب (al-ghālib): That which is dominant in conjecture, treated as certainty in legal rulings.
الضرر (al-ḍarar): Harm or injury that is feared, which becomes a valid excuse.
الاضطرار (al-iḍṭirār): Necessity that permits what is otherwise prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Whenever she wants to beautify herself.
B) When she has a strong fear of headache or eye pain without it.
C) Only if her husband's heirs permit it.
D) It is never permissible.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that the dominant conjecture is treated as certainty allows a woman in iddah to use oil for medical necessity, provided she does not intend adornment.

The Wajib Nature of Ihdad and Its Cause
Establishes the ruling and its cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of ihdad, explain its cause (ʿilla), and apply it to determine who must observe it.

Core Idea
Ihdad is wajib to express sorrow for losing the blessing of marriage; only a widow of a valid marriage observes it.

The Hanafi school derives the obligation of mourning (ihdad) from a clear legal cause: the loss of the blessing of marriage. This lesson unpacks that cause and its implications. You will learn why ihdad is not merely a ritual but a response to a specific blessing, which then excludes those who never possessed that blessing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that ihdad is wajib. Note that it is an obligation for a specific group: women in iddah of a valid marriage whose husband has died.
The ruling is stated clearly at the start.
2
Extract the ʿilla (cause)
The text says it is wajib 'as a display of sorrow over the loss of the blessing of marriage.' The cause is the loss of that blessing, not merely the death itself.
The word 'nimat' (blessing) is key.
3
Apply the ʿilla to determine scope
Since the cause is limited to those who had a valid marriage blessing, ihdad applies only to widows of valid marriages. Those who never enjoyed a valid marriage (e.g., umm walad, fasid nikah) or lack capacity (minor, insane) are excluded.
This logical connection shows the precision of Hanafi reasoning.
4
Confirm the source authority
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, cited in al-Hidayah and al-Ikhtiyar. It is the mufta bihi position with no intra-Hanafi dispute.
This gives the ruling its weight in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۲) إِنَّ الْحِدَادَ يَجِبُّ إِظْهَارًا لِلتَّأَسُّفِ عَلَى فَوْتِ نِعْمَةِ النِّكَاحِ. ترجمہ: سوگ واجب ہے نکاح کی نعمت کے فوت ہونے پر افسوس ظاہر کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عورت پر جو حداد یعنی سوگ منانا واجب ہے اس کی علت نکاح کی نعمت کے فوت ہونے پر افسوس کا اظہار کرنا ہے، کیونکہ نکاح کی وجہ سے عورت کونان نفقہ اور عفت وغیرہ حاصل ہوتے ہیں تو نکاح یہ عورت کے لئے بڑی نعمت ہے ، لہذ اسوگ منانے کی علت اسی نعمت کے فوت ہونے پر اظہار افسوس ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ ام ولد اور نکاح فاسد کی صورت میں عورت پر سوگ کرنا واجب نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ سوگ نکاح کی نعمت کے زوال پر ہوتا ہے ،ام ولد اور نکاح فاسد والی عورت کے حق میں نعمت نکاح زائل نہیں ہوئی ہے، اس لئے اظہار افسوس کے لئے سوگ واجب نہیں ہے، چونکہ زیب وزینت کی اباحت اصل ہے، لہذا یہ حکم اپنی اصل پر باقی رہے گا۔
وَلَا إِحْدَادَ عَلَى صَغِيرَةٍ وَلَا مَجْنُونَةٍ لِعَدَمِ الْخِطَابِ وَلَأَنَّهَا عِبَادَةٌ حَتَّى لَا تَجِبَ عَلَى الْكَافِرَةِ، بِخِلَافِ الْأَمَةِ لِأَنَّهَا أَهْلْ لِلْعِبَادَاتِ وَلَيْسَ فِيهَا إِبْطَالُ حَقِّ الْمَوْلَى، وَلَيْسَ فِي عِدَّةِ النِّكَاحِ الْفَاسِدِ إِحْدَادٌ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُتَأَسَفُ عَلَى زَوَالِهِ لأنَّهُ وَاجِبُ الزَّوَالِ وَلَأَنَّهُ نِقْمَةٌ فَرَوَالُهُ نِعْمَةٌ. الاختيار لتعليل المختار كتاب الطلاق، باب العدة، فصل في الحداد، ج ۳ ص ۷۸ ۱، ط: مطبعة المجلس القاهرة الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب العدة، فصل، ج ۲ ص ۴۳۴، ط: رحمانیه
(112) Indeed, mourning (ihdad) is wajib as a display of sorrow over the loss of the blessing of marriage. Translation: Mourning is wajib because of showing sorrow over the loss of the blessing of marriage. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that the mourning (ihdad) wajib on a woman, its cause is to show sorrow over the loss of the blessing of marriage, because through marriage a woman obtains maintenance, chastity, etc., so marriage is a great blessing for a woman. Therefore, the cause of mourning is the expression of sorrow over the loss of this blessing. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is explaining that for an umm walad (slave-concubine who bore a child) and in the case of a fasid (invalid) marriage, mourning is not wajib, because mourning is for the loss of the blessing of marriage; for the woman of umm walad and fasid nikah, the blessing of marriage has not been lost, therefore mourning for expressing sorrow is not wajib. Since permissibility of adornment is the original rule, this ruling remains upon its origin. And there is no mourning upon a minor or insane woman due to absence of legal capacity (khitab), and because it is an act of worship (ibadah) so that it is not obligatory on a disbelieving woman, contrary to a slave-woman (amah) because she is capable of acts of worship and there is no annulment of the master's right in it. There is no mourning in the iddah of fasid nikah, because one does not sorrow over its removal, since it is necessarily removed, and because it is an affliction (niqma) so its removal is a blessing. [From al-Ikhtiyar li-Ta'lil al-Mukhtar, Book of Divorce, Chapter of Iddah, Section on Ihdad, vol. 3 p. 781, Matba'at al-Majlis al-Qahira; al-Hidayah, Book of Divorce, Chapter of Iddah, section, vol. 2 p. 434, Rahmaniyyah]
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage highlights the 'illa of ihdad: it is an expression of sorrow for the loss of the blessing of marriage. Therefore, it only applies when a valid marriage blessing was lost. For umm walad, the master's death ends the slave-concubinage, not a marriage. For fasid nikah, the marriage is invalid and must be terminated, so its loss is not sorrowful. Also, minor and insane women lack full obligation, and disbelievers are not addressed by this worship. A female slave (amah) does observe ihdad because she has legal capacity and her husband's right is not annulled. The Hanafi school thus confines ihdad to widows of valid marriages only. Sources from al-Ikhtiyar (which is a matn of the Hanafi school) and al-Hidayah confirm this. Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الحداد (al-ihdād): Mourning observed by a widow, refraining from adornment and using perfume.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-concubine who has borne a child to her master.
نكاح فاسد (nikāḥ fāsid): A marriage that is defective due to missing a condition or presence of a prohibition, but not invalid (batil) in substance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal cause (ʿilla) that makes ihdad wajib according to the Hanafi school?
A) The death of the husband
B) The loss of the blessing of marriage
C) The iddah period
D) The need to express grief publicly

Key Takeaway
Ihdad is wajib only on widows of valid marriages because its cause is the loss of that blessing; those who never had a valid marriage or lack capacity are exempt.

Exceptions to Ihdad: Umm Walad, Fasid Nikah, and Others
Lists exceptions and their rationales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the exceptions to ihdad and explain the legal reason for each exception.

Core Idea
The blessing of marriage is absent for umm walad and fasid nikah, so no sorrow; minor and insane lack capacity; non-Muslim is not addressed.

Building on the cause of ihdad, the Hanafi school explicitly exempts several categories of women. This lesson examines each exception: umm walad (slave-concubine), fasid nikah, minor, insane, and non-Muslim. Understanding these exceptions helps avoid misapplication of the ruling.

Guided Path
1
List all exceptions mentioned in the passage
Note each exception: umm walad (implied by the principle), minor, insane, non-Muslim, and women in iddah of fasid nikah.
The text explicitly mentions minor, insane, disbeliever, and fasid nikah. Umm walad is derived from the principle.
2
For each exception, identify why the ʿilla does not apply
The ʿilla is loss of blessing of valid marriage. Umm walad and fasid nikah never had that blessing. Minor and insane lack capacity. Non-Muslim is not addressed by this ibadah.
Each exception has a distinct rationale.
3
Note the case of the amah (slave woman)
Contrary to some misconceptions, a married slave woman (amah) does observe ihdad because she has legal capacity and her marriage is valid.
This shows that slavery does not automatically exempt from ihdad.
4
Apply the list to real cases
Given a woman with a certain status, determine if she falls into an exception.
Practice with scenarios.

وَلَا إِحْدَادَ عَلَى صَغِيرَةٍ وَلَا مَجْنُونَةٍ لِعَدَمِ الْخِطَابِ وَلَأَنَّهَا عِبَادَةٌ حَتَّى لَا تَجِبَ عَلَى الْكَافِرَةِ، بِخِلَافِ الْأَمَةِ لِأَنَّهَا أَهْلْ لِلْعِبَادَاتِ وَلَيْسَ فِيهَا إِبْطَالُ حَقِّ الْمَوْلَى، وَلَيْسَ فِي عِدَّةِ النِّكَاحِ الْفَاسِدِ إِحْدَادٌ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُتَأَسَفُ عَلَى زَوَالِهِ لأنَّهُ وَاجِبُ الزَّوَالِ وَلَأَنَّهُ نِقْمَةٌ فَرَوَالُهُ نِعْمَةٌ. الاختيار لتعليل المختار كتاب الطلاق، باب العدة، فصل في الحداد، ج ۳ ص ۷۸ ۱، ط: مطبعة المجلس القاهرة الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب العدة، فصل، ج ۲ ص ۴۳۴، ط: رحمانیه
(112) Indeed, mourning (ihdad) is wajib as a display of sorrow over the loss of the blessing of marriage. Excuses Affecting Worship: Widow's Residence in Iddah
Explaining the principle that excuses affect worship and its application to a widow moving from the husband's house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that excuses affect worship to determine the permissibility of a widow moving during iddah.

Core Idea
A genuine excuse can lift an obligation in worship, such as a widow's duty to stay in the husband's house.

In Hanafi fiqh, acts of worship are not absolute; they can be modified or waived when a valid excuse (udhr) exists. This lesson explores that principle through the case of a widow during iddah. We will see how the obligation to remain in the marital home can fall when hardship arises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
First, recognize that staying in the husband's house during iddah is an act of worship (ibadah). The default ruling is that it is obligatory (wajib) for the widow.
This is based on the Quranic command to remain in the house during iddah.
2
State the principle governing excuses
The Hanafi school holds that legitimately recognized excuses can affect acts of worship, either by making them permissible (mubah) to omit or by dropping the obligation entirely.
This is a general usul principle, not limited to iddah.
3
Identify the specific excuse in the case
In the passage, the excuse is that the widow's share of the house is insufficient and the heirs expel her. Other valid excuses include fear for property, fear of collapse, or inability to pay rent.
The excuse must be genuine and not a mere preference.
4
Apply the principle to the case
Since the excuse is valid, the obligation to stay is lifted (saqit). Therefore, the widow may move to another safe and secluded place to complete her iddah.
The act of worship (staying) is not invalidated; only the requirement to do it in that specific location falls.
5
Consider the practical consequence (thamarah)
The practical result is that the widow's iddah remains valid even if she moves, provided the move is due to a valid excuse. Without the excuse, moving would be a violation.
This shows the flexibility in Hanafi fiqh to accommodate hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۳) وَالْعِبَادَاتُ تُؤَثِرُ فِيهَا الْأَعْذَارُ. ترجمہ: عبادات میں اعزار مؤثر ہوتے ہیں۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اعذار شریعہ جتنے بھی ہیں یہ عبادات میں مؤثر ہوتے ہیں ، بایں طور کے عذر کی بناء پر عبادت ساقط ہو جاتی ہے، مثلاً حالت حیض میں نماز ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر متوفی عنہا ز و جہا کا حصہ میت کے گھر میں اتنا ہے کہ وہ قلت کی وجہ سے اس کے لئے کافی نہیں ہے اور ورثا ء نے اس کو اپنے حصے سے نکال دیا، تو اس صورت میں یہ عورت یہاں سے کسی دوسری جگہ منتقل ہو سکتی ہے، کیونکہ اس انتقال میں عذر ہے، میت کے گھر میں دورانِ عدت ٹھہرنا یہ عبادت ہے، اور عذر عبادت میں مؤثر ہوتا ہے، لہذا یہاں بھی اس عورت کا یہ عذر مؤثر ہوگا اور اس کی وجہ سے عبادت یعنی گھر میں ٹھہر نا ساقط ہو جائے گا، اور اس کے لئے کسی دوسرے محفوظ اور پردہ دار مقام پر عدت گزارنا درست ہے۔
فإن كان نصيبها من (دار زوجها الميت لا يكفيها) لضيقه فأخرجها الورثة من نصيبهم انتقلت إلى حيث شاءت ، لأن هذا الانتقال بعذر، والعبادات تؤثر فيها الأعذار، وصار كما إذا خافت على متاعها، أو خافت سقوط المنزل، أو كانت فيه بأجر ولا تجد ما تؤديه. اللباب في شرح الكتاب: كتاب العدة، ج ۳ ص ۸۶، ط: المكتبة العلمية
(113) Acts of worship are affected by excuses. Translation: Excuses affect acts of worship. Explanation: The summary of the mentioned principle is that whatever excuses exist in the Shari'ah, they are effective in acts of worship, in the sense that due to the excuse, the worship becomes nullified (saaqit). For example, in the state of menstruation, prayer is dropped. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if the share of the deceased husband's house for the widow is so little that due to its smallness it is not sufficient for her, and the heirs release her share, then in this case this woman can move to another place, because this move is due to an excuse. Staying in the deceased's house during the iddah is an act of worship, and an excuse affects worship. Therefore, here also this woman's excuse will be effective and due to it the worship, i.e., staying in the house, becomes waived, and it is correct for her to complete her iddah in another safe and secluded place. [If her share of the house of her deceased husband is not sufficient for her due to its constriction, and the heirs expel her from their share, she may move wherever she wishes, because this move is due to an excuse, and acts of worship are affected by excuses. This is like when she fears for her belongings, or fears the collapse of the house, or she is there on rent and cannot pay it. From al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, Book of Iddah, vol. 3 p. 86, al-Maktabah al-Ilmiyyah]
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage establishes the principle that excuses (a'dhar) such as hardship, necessity, or fear can lift or modify obligations in worship. The specific application: a widow's obligation to stay in the deceased husband's house for iddah is an act of worship (specifically ibadah as it is commanded by Allah). Therefore, if her share is too small and heirs expel her, she may move. This is a dispensation (rukhsah) based on the principle. The Hanafi school gives weight to such excuses even in matters of worship, provided the excuse is genuine. The source from al-Lubab (a commentary) clarifies the conditions. Authority weight: This principle is well-established in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الأعذار (al-aʿdhār): Legally recognized excuses that can lift or modify obligations, especially in worship.
العبادات (al-ʿibādāt): Acts of worship ordained by Allah, including prayer, fasting, and in this context, staying in the husband's house during iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for a widow being allowed to move from her deceased husband's house during iddah?
A) She can move freely as she wishes.
B) The principle that excuses affect worship, combined with the hardship of insufficient space.
C) She must move if her share is small.
D) Moving is always preferred.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that excuses affect worship permits a widow to move during iddah if a genuine hardship exists, such as insufficient share or fear for safety.

Custody Follows the Mother's Lineage
States and explains the principle that custody follows maternal lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that custody rights are traced through the mother's lineage and apply it to determine priority among female relatives.

Core Idea
Custody follows the mother's line: maternal relatives prevail over paternal relatives.

In matters of child custody, the Hanafi school establishes a clear hierarchy based on lineage. This passage from Usool E Hidayah explains that the right of custody (hadanah) is derived from the mother's side, giving preference to maternal relatives over paternal ones even if the maternal relative is more distant in degree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling principle
The passage states: 'The authority of custody of the child is obtained from the side of the mothers.' This is the foundational rule.
2
Understand the implication
This means maternal relatives (e.g., maternal grandmother, maternal aunt) take precedence over paternal relatives (e.g., paternal grandmother, paternal aunt).
The preference is based on lineage side, not necessarily degree of relationship.
3
Apply to a concrete scenario
If the mother is absent, the maternal grandmother is more entitled to custody than the paternal grandmother, even if the maternal grandmother is a more distant relative in terms of proximity.
This is a direct application of the principle.
4
Distinguish from guardianship
Note that custody (hadanah) is about physical care and upbringing, while guardianship (wilayah) about legal authority often lies with the father. The principle here applies only to hadanah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حضانة الولد ومن أحق به
(١١٤) إِنَّ وِلَايَةَ حِضَانَةِ الْوَلَدِ تُسْتَفَادُ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْأُمَّهَاتِ . ترجمہ: بچے کی پرورش کرنے کی ولایت ماؤں کی طرف سے آتی ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بچے کی پرورش کرنے کا حق پہلے ان عورتوں کو حاصل ہے جو اس بچے کی ماں کی طرف سے قریبی رشتہ دار ہیں ، مثلاً نانی ، خالہ اور بہن وغیرہ۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر بچے کی ماں نہیں ہے تو پھر نانی پرورش کرنے کی زیادہ حقدار ہے بنسبت دادی کے ، اگر چہ وہ نانی بعید ہی کیوں نہ ہو، کیونکہ یہ پرورش کی جو ولایت ہے یہ ماں کی طرف سے ہے۔ ماں کی طرف سے جو اس بچے کی قریبی رشتہ دار ہیں ان کو زیادہ حق حاصل ہے بنسبت ان عورتوں کے جو باپ کی طرف سے اس بچے کے رشتہ دار ہیں، تو نانی چونکہ اس بچے کی ماں کی طرف سے رشتہ دار ہے لہذا نانی زیادہ حقدار ہوگی بنسبت دادی کے، کیونکہ دادی کے ساتھ اس بچے کا رشتہ باپ کی طرف سے ہے۔
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب حضانة الولد ومن أحق به، ج ۲ ص ۴۳۹، ط: رحمانیه
الاختيار لتعليل المختار كتاب الطلاق، باب النفقة باب الحضانة، ج ۴ ص ۱۵، ط: مطبعة المجلس القاهرة
The chapter on custody of the child and who is more entitled to it. (114) Indeed, the authority of custody of the child is obtained from the side of the mothers. Translation: The authority to raise the child comes from the side of the mothers. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that the right to raise the child is first given to those women who are close relatives from the child's mother's side, such as the maternal grandmother, maternal aunt, and sister, etc. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if the child's mother is not present, then the maternal grandmother is more entitled to custody than the paternal grandmother, even if that maternal grandmother is distant, because this custody authority is from the mother's side. Those who are close relatives from the mother's side have more right than those women who are relatives from the father's side. Therefore, since the maternal grandmother is a relative from the child's mother's side, she is more entitled than the paternal grandmother, because the paternal grandmother's relation to the child is through the father. Al-Hidayah, Book of Divorce, Chapter of Custody and Who is More Entitled to It, vol. 2, p. 439, Rahimaniyya edition. Al-Ikhtiyar li Ta'lil al-Mukhtar, Book of Divorce, Chapter of Nafaqah Chapter of Custody, vol. 4, p. 15, al-Majlis al-Qahira press.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage from Usool E Hidayah presents the ruling principle that the right of custody (hadanah) is derived from the mother's side. The author explains that maternal relatives take precedence over paternal ones. For example, the maternal grandmother is preferred over the paternal grandmother even if she is more distant in degree. This is because the authority for custody comes from the mother's lineage. The text also provides practical examples: if the mother is absent, the maternal grandmother, then maternal aunt, etc., are prioritized over paternal relatives. The principle is from the Hidayah, and the commentary clarifies its application.

Key Terms
ولاية الحضانة (wilāyat al-ḥaḍānah): The legal authority to raise and care for a child.
حضانة (ḥaḍānah): Custody and physical care of a child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle, who is more entitled to custody: the maternal grandmother or the paternal grandmother?
A) The paternal grandmother, because she is the father's mother.
B) The maternal grandmother, because custody authority comes from the mother's side.
C) Both are equally entitled.
D) The one who lives closer to the child.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, child custody (hadanah) is prioritised for maternal female relatives over paternal ones, because the right of custody flows from the mother's lineage.
